Local News

Sino-British Wireless Telegraph Service Contract Signed

Based on Equality and Reciprocity, Term is Ten Years

Ministry of Communications Has Ordered Equipment, Service to Be Available Next Year

Will Enable International Telegraph and Telephone Communications

Since the establishment of the International Radio Station, the Ministry of Communications has recovered rights and interests for China's telecommunications industry, no small feat. During the Shanghai War, communication was maintained consistently without interruption. The station currently has direct circuits to the United States, Germany, France, Switzerland, the Philippines, Java, Saigon, Hong Kong, and other locations. However, there is no direct circuit to the United Kingdom. Recognizing that London telegrams account for a significant portion of international telegram traffic, the Ministry of Communications deemed this direct communication to be of utmost importance and initiated the process. It has ordered two sets of 20-kilowatt wireless telegraph and telephone equipment from Marconi Company, totaling approximately 800,000 yuan in national currency. The funds will be sourced from the income from international wireless telegraph fees. According to reliable sources, the Sino-British Wireless Telegraph Service Contract has been formally signed by the Ministry of Communications and the British Imperial and International Communications Company. Previously, the contract faced considerable difficulties due to cable issues, and negotiations had been ongoing for years without resolution. Its realization this time will further consolidate the foundation of China's international wireless communications. The content of the contract is reportedly similar to the previously signed contracts with the United States, Germany, and France, based on the principle of equality and reciprocity, totaling twenty articles. Among them, the most important is the second article: "Both parties shall use all reasonable means to solicit business for the aforementioned circuits and endeavor to maintain symmetrical traffic on the aforementioned circuits." The term of the contract is ten years, effective from the date when the new equipment begins service next year. It is also reported that the wireless equipment is not only capable of international telegraph communications but also international telephone communications. In the future, direct telephone calls will be possible between Shanghai and London, and between Shanghai and San Francisco, further facilitating Sino-foreign communications.

Disaster Area Rehabilitation Committee Requests Exemption from Local Taxes

Until Restoration to Pre-War Conditions

The Shanghai Disaster Area Industrial and Commercial Rehabilitation Committee submitted a document to the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday, stating: "Regarding the promulgation of measures to exempt disaster areas from taxes, they are not truly beneficial. We earnestly request your review and approval to exempt them from local taxes until pre-war conditions are restored, in order to facilitate rehabilitation." The document stated that the committee believed that to rehabilitate the disaster area, the first priority should be the exemption from national and local taxes. A request to this effect had previously been submitted for your consideration. However, upon reading the newspapers, it was learned that the tax exemption measures announced by your office only included the exemption of advertising tax for two seasons, ferry boats, etc., from the date of resumption of business, and the exemption of rent for the first and second categories of civilian residences for two, three, and four months, respectively. It is noted that the Japanese invasion of Shanghai began on January 28th, and the Japanese began their retreat in mid-May. Even now, the withdrawal is not complete. The area was ravaged by the Japanese for four full months. Yet, the exemption from advertising tax is only for two seasons, and the rent exemption for the first and second categories of civilian residences is only for three months. All other taxes must be paid from the date of resumption of business. The people's payment of taxes is originally for the protection of the government. During the Japanese invasion of Shanghai, the lives and property of the affected areas were subject to arbitrary killing and plunder. The government lost its ability to protect them. Since the government has lost its ability to protect, and the people are unable to conduct business peacefully, even if the government wants to collect taxes, it will be impossible to collect. It is obviously not appropriate to call the uncollectible taxes 'exemptions' to show benevolence to the disaster victims. Uninformed people may think that the government is feigning benevolence. Although this may seem an overstatement, the fact is that this exemption measure is of no benefit to rehabilitation. It is therefore necessary to submit another application, requesting your review and approval to exempt local taxes until pre-war conditions are restored, which would be in the public interest."

Resolving War Zone Debts in a Spirit of Mutual Understanding and Concession

Creditors Should Accommodate Within Possible Limits

Debtors Should Fulfill Obligations to the Best of Their Ability

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has sent letters to various industries to resolve the issue of debts in the war zone, stating: "We are writing to inform you that our Jiangwan branch office has previously written to us regarding the debts owed by businesses in the district. For those who owe money, the creditors may not be able to waive the debts simply because they have suffered from the disaster. For those who are owed money, it is difficult to expect them to repay the debts when the entire town has been devastated. We request that you provide guidance on how to resolve this issue and issue a notice for implementation." This matter was discussed at the 92nd Standing Committee meeting, and it was decided to solicit opinions from various trade associations and offices before compiling them and submitting them to the Third Members' General Assembly for discussion. Subsequently, various industries provided feedback, including suggestions that if businesses can reorganize and resume operations but are unable to repay maturing debts due to depleted resources, they should be allowed to issue limited-term promissory notes for installment payments; that debts owed to and by people within the Jiangwan war zone should be deferred for up to three months with installment payments, but all transactions must be in cash until the previous debts are cleared; that if businesses have not resumed operations but their assets have not been lost, the debts should be reduced after verification; that those who owe money should make installment payments, giving priority to those owed money who are in the same area and have suffered similar losses; that those who are owed money should make every effort to collect debts, but those who owe money in the same disaster area should be allowed to make installment payments; and that debtors who have suffered actual losses should be understood and tolerated after verification, while those who are concealing assets and evading debts should be strictly pursued. Although the views differed, all had their reasons. These views were listed and submitted to the Third Members' General Assembly for discussion. At the meeting, it was decided that the Chamber of Commerce should advise both creditors and debtors to seek understanding and solutions under the protection of the law and considering the special circumstances. The Executive Committee was instructed to handle the matter according to these principles. The recent Shanghai war occurred precisely at the time when accounts were being settled at the end of the year. The devastation was particularly severe. If businesses do not help each other, they will inevitably collapse together. Creditors should negotiate flexible solutions within their possible limits to allow debtors to gradually resume operations. Debtors should also faithfully fulfill their obligations to the best of their ability, so that creditors are not forced into a desperate situation while accommodating others. Mutual understanding and concession will allow everyone to move towards a brighter future. In light of the Jiangwan branch's request for guidance, it is impossible to apply a single standard due to the varying degrees of disaster, creditworthiness, and assets. Instead, each household should consult with each other based on their usual dealings. We hereby issue this notice, hoping that you will inform your members of the spirit of mutual assistance and concession and handle the matter accordingly. This is our sincere hope."

Ma Zhanshan Cables Report on Anti-Japanese Struggle

Ma Zhanshan cables to all circles in Shanghai: "General Zhu Ziqiao, Mr. Huang Jinrong, Mr. Xu Jilong, Mr. Du Yuesheng, Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Mr. Wu Shan, and all comrades: Zhanshan swore an oath last month and set off, as reported in a previous telegram. Prior plans were made to divide our forces and coordinate with the Jilin Army and the armies along the Hu-Hai line, and the Ding and Li units to attack Harbin. Just as we were about to capture it, the Japanese suddenly landed a large number of troops from warships in Bayan, attacking our army's left flank and occupying Hailun, attempting to cut off our retreat. They engaged in rape, arson, and murder, acting with extreme cruelty. The righteous army returned and fought fiercely for more than twenty days. Zhanshan rushed to the front to supervise the troops, boosting their morale. On the evening of the [blank]th of this month, we attacked Hailun and the Catholic Church northwest of Hailun at 10 PM, breaching both at around 11 PM. Street fighting ensued, with hand-to-hand combat lasting about three hours, and we nearly repelled the enemy. It is estimated that we killed over 150 enemies at both locations, captured over 100 rifles, and killed 80 horses. Our officers and soldiers suffered over 40 casualties. We are currently pursuing and clearing the area. Further details will be reported later. Reporting this first. Ma Zhanshan, seal."

British Also Advocate Convening a Round Table Conference

Phrasing Quite Clever, Reuters, London, 25th: "Today, The Times published a letter from Conservative Member of Parliament Walter Runciman, warmly supporting the Shanghai and Hong Kong Chamber of Commerce's proposal to convene a round table conference to discuss Shanghai's future. He stated that Britain is not currently involved in any plans to forcibly demand concessions from China that China does not want to grant. However, the issue of Shanghai's future predates the Sino-Japanese dispute. While a ceasefire is sufficient to clear the air, it is not a final solution. He believes that some members of the ruling Kuomintang in Nanjing sincerely desire to use this ceasefire as the starting point for a new situation. The greatest source of power for the National Government is the stability of Shanghai, and this is an opportunity to achieve this goal."

Journalists' Association Established

Total of 134 Members Attended

Thirty-Six Executive and Supervisory Committee Members Elected

The Shanghai Journalists' Association held its inaugural meeting at the YMCA on Eight Immortals Bridge at 2:00 PM yesterday. 134 members attended, passed the constitution, and elected executive and supervisory committee members. Details are as follows:

Meeting Officials: The presidium was publicly elected as Yan Esheng, He Xiya, Ma Chong, Hang Shijun, Zhao Junhao; Recorders: Jin Huating, Xu Chizhen; Master of Ceremonies: Wu Zhongyi; Venue Staff: Sun Daosheng, Yu Kongwo; Ticket Inspectors: Jiang Zongdao, Jiang Jianhou, Sun Daosheng, Yao Gengkui, Wang Anzhi, Zhou Lianze; Reception: handled by all members of the preparatory committee; Marshals and inspectors of admission tickets: jointly handled by the Boy Scouts of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Meeting Agenda: (1) Public Election of the Presidium; (2) Paying Respects to the Party, National Flag, and the Portrait of the Premier; (3) Chairman Reads the Premier's Will; (4) Chairman's Opening Remarks; (5) Report on Preparatory Work by the Preparatory Committee; (6) Addresses by Representatives of the Municipal Government and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs; (7) Adoption of the Constitution; (8) Election of Officers; (9) Discussion of Proposals; (10) Photo Session and Adjournment.

Meeting Scene: After the opening ceremony and salutations, Chairman Yan Esheng delivered the opening remarks, stating: "The organization of Shanghai journalists began more than twelve years ago, at which time it was called the Shanghai Journalists' Association. I still recall that when the association held its inaugural meeting, there were only twenty members. Later, the association was reorganized into the Federation, and the number of members increased. This time, it was reorganized into the Journalists' Association, with a registered membership of as many as 197 people. This increase in the number of journalist members is sufficient to demonstrate the development of the journalist profession. The task of the Journalists' Association is to seek the development of the journalism profession and the improvement of the status of journalists, as the two are interrelated, like the two wheels of a car. If the status of journalists cannot be improved, then the development of the journalism profession will be abnormal. Conversely, if the journalism profession cannot be developed, then the status of journalists cannot be improved. Journalists bear a great responsibility to the country and society. Journalists are well aware of this and need not be praised by others. But great responsibility must be borne by great ability. From the perspective of the individual, if the individual's ability is strengthened, then the individual's service efficiency will increase. From the perspective of the whole, if the ability of the journalism community is strengthened, then the journalism profession will develop. However, strength comes from solidarity. The organization of the Journalists' Association seeks the solidarity of the journalism community so that it can generate sufficient ability and develop its cause." Jiang Jianhou, on behalf of the preparatory committee, reported on the preparatory work. Next, Chen Kecheng, representative of the Municipal Government, and Chen Lengseng, representative of the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, delivered speeches. The meeting then began to discuss the constitution, revising it article by article. After the principles were passed, the articles were handed over to the executive committee for processing. After all the discussions were completed, the elections began, using a double-named cumulative voting method to elect fifteen executive committee members, seven alternates, nine supervisory committee members, and five alternates. Next, the meeting discussed proposals. Regarding the job security proposal, it was decided to organize a specialized committee to handle it. Also, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Boy Scouts provided diligent service at the meeting, and it was decided to send a formal letter of thanks in the name of the Journalists' Association. Finally, a photo session was held and the meeting was adjourned.

Elected Officials: (1) Fifteen Executive Committee Members: Elected were Ma Chong, 61 votes; Yan Esheng, 58 votes; He Xiya, 50 votes; Jin Xiongbo, 45 votes; Zhao Junhao, 43 votes; Yu Kongwo, 43 votes; Hang Shijun, 41 votes; Jin Huating, 39 votes; Qu Shaoyi, 39 votes; Qian Cangshuo, 39 votes; Jiang Jianhou, 37 votes; Du Gang, 37 votes; Sun Daosheng, 34 votes; Hu Zhongchi, 30 votes; Wu Zhongyi, 29 votes. (2) Seven Alternate Executive Committee Members: Qian Hua, 28 votes; Xu Chizhen, 26 votes; Zhu Chaoran, 24 votes; Jiang Zongdao, 24 votes; Zhang Zhihan, 21 votes; Wang Anzhi, 20 votes; Shen Qiuyan, 19 votes. (3) Nine Supervisory Committee Members: Yan Duhe, 42 votes; Hu Pu'an, 25 votes; Li Haoran, 21 votes; Guo Butao, 20 votes; Chen Dazai, 19 votes; Zhou Shoujuan, 18 votes; Gu Zhizhong, 15 votes; Hu Hanzhu, 14 votes; Guan Jiu'an, 13 votes. (4) Five Alternate Supervisory Committee Members: Tang Huiping, 13 votes; Jiang Hongjiao, 12 votes; Li Zutang, 10 votes; Wen Gongda, 10 votes; Wu Zhiping, 10 votes.

Hongkou Silk Factories Striked Yesterday

Participants Include Yi Chang, Yun Cheng, Xiang Cheng and Other Three Factories

The Reason for the Strike Was Opposition to the Factory's Wage Cuts

Yi Chang on Wuzhou Road, Yun Cheng and Xiang Cheng on Tiantong Road, and other three silk factories in Hongkou, suddenly experienced a strike wave starting yesterday noon, with more than 1,000 people participating. After learning of this, other silk factories separately reported to the police station and requested protection, so it did not spread, but the situation is very serious. The details are recorded below.

Reasons for the Strike: There are more than 20 silk factories in the Hongkou district of this city. Since the downturn in European sales last year and the sudden drop in the silk market, 60% to 70% of them have suspended operations. The sudden outbreak of the Shanghai war made it difficult for the factories that had not suspended operations to continue. After the Sino-Japanese agreement was reached, more than a dozen factories, including Yi Chang, Tong Wei, Yu Jing, Ren Ji, Yun Cheng, Xiang Cheng, Tong Yi, Hou Fu, Wei Yu, and Fu Lun Heng, resumed operations one after another. Unexpectedly, when these factories started work, seeing that the workers were eager to resume work, they extended the working hours from 11 hours to 12 hours, and the wages were reduced from 58 cents to 42 cents. All silkworm moth upgrades were cancelled, and wages were reduced to 70% of the original level and calculated daily. At that time, the workers repeatedly endured the pain due to the harsh environment, hoping for a turnaround in the silk market before trying to find a solution. Recently, the workers of Yi Chang and other factories felt that their income was meager and difficult to make ends meet. They reported to the union and seriously negotiated with the capitalists, demanding the restoration of their original wages. Unexpectedly, Chen, the person in charge of the union, initially told them to wait patiently for negotiations and not to act rashly, and then flattered the capitalists. The workers could no longer bear it and announced a strike at 12:00 noon yesterday. After the workers of Yi Chang factory went on strike, all the workers rushed to Yun Cheng and Xiang Cheng factories on Tiantong Road, demanding that the workers of the factory take the same action. Seeing that the situation was not good, the factory authorities announced a shutdown and released the male and female workers in the factory, so they also joined the strike. In total, the number of strikers was about 1,000.

Factories on Guard: After the workers of Yi Chang and other three factories went on strike, Ren Ji Silk Factory on Dixiwei Road was afraid of being affected and immediately reported to the Third Sub-Bureau of the Fifth District and requested protection. The precinct dispatched patrol police to the scene to suppress the strike. The workers did not take action when they saw the security. At the gates of Tong Wei and Yu Jing factories on Wuzhou Road, the Harbin police sent a large number of Chinese and foreign detectives to guard the area closely, and no incidents occurred. Tong Yi Silk Factory on Xiangyanqiao Road and Hou Fu Silk Factory on Zhangjia Lane were still operating as usual.

Authorities Investigate: After the outbreak of the strike, the Party and government agencies will send personnel to investigate today in order to find out the truth so as to deal with it and prevent the strike from expanding and affecting social security.

National Medicine Industry Facing Strike Trend

Warning Has Been Issued to Capitalists

Municipal Party Department Is Doing Its Utmost to Prevent It

The situation of all employees in the national medicine industry in this city was very serious yesterday, with a trend of strikes. The Municipal Party Department is properly planning and doing its utmost to prevent it. The various situations are recorded separately below.

Warning to Capitalists: The Council of the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, according to the resolutions of the members' representatives meeting, sent a stern letter yesterday to Feng Cunren, Cai Tongde, Ye Tiande and other three pharmacies, which were the first to undermine labor-capital conditions and refuse outside field substitutes, warning them not to arbitrarily undermine the conditions, notifying all members to unanimously oppose them, and preparing to issue a declaration refuting the illegal actions of the guild. As for the Salary Increase Campaign Committee, it was announced yesterday to have been established, and the first committee meeting will be held in the shortest possible time to discuss how to proceed.

Capitalist Attitude: Those concerned about the case, in order to understand the other side of the situation, specially visited Zhang Meian, executive committee member of the National Medicine Industry Association and director of the secretariat, yesterday and had the following conversation: (Question) What is the inside story of your industry's union opposing the division of inside and outside fields and refusing outside field substitutes? Please show a rough estimate. (Answer) The case of dividing the boundaries of inside and outside field clerks in this industry was handled by this association according to the instructions of the Ministry of Industry and the Central Training Department, and not by this association's own initiative to divide the union's organization, because in addition to the inside field clerks in the national medicine industry in this city who have some skills and can join the union as members, the outside field clerks are completely in the position of commercial employees and should belong to the guild according to law. The Ministry's order to divide is indeed most appropriate. This association, in order to execute the order, has resolved through the executive committee meeting to notify the outside field clerks to register first so as to start the

Page 14

Division. There is nothing inappropriate in the handling. If the union opposes the division, it should state the reasons and apply to the Ministry of Industry and other departments for relief. That is the right way. If it is used to blame the capitalists and attempt to restrain the capitalists through strikes, I am afraid that it will not be understood by society. As for refusing outside field substitutes, the reason is also here. Since the outside field clerks should belong to the guild according to law, when each store needs to use substitutes because the outside field clerks return home, the store has full power to freely hire them. How can the union refuse to agree with the store and arbitrarily send substitutes to deprive the store of its due rights? Moreover, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has also strictly ordered the union to stop the illegal practice of arbitrarily sending outside field substitutes. What is the union blaming? (Question) I heard that the union has the intention of capitalists undermining labor-capital conditions. What is the truth? (Answer) The labor-capital treatment conditions of this industry were signed in the spring of the 16th year of the Republic of China. At that time, various industrial and commercial laws and regulations had not been promulgated, and the contract was not based on any basis, so the content was very obstructive. The central government considered that this condition conflicted with the current laws and regulations, and disputes would not end if it was not improved. Therefore, it specially ordered the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Party Department, and the Municipal Government to properly revise it in order to achieve perfection. However, although the order has been issued for more than a year, the competent authorities have not been able to do so due to the current situation and the stability relationship. Now, the colleagues in our industry, because they cannot bear the pain of illegal private restraints, have unanimously requested this association to urge the competent authorities to expedite the revision in order to relieve the merchants' difficulties. This is just urging the handling of the pending case, and there is no destruction to speak of. (Question) The union resolved to demand a salary increase of ten yuan per person per month. Do your colleagues in the association accept this? (Answer) This issue is of great importance, and I dare not answer it without authorization, but in view of the current state of commercial decline and the difficult situation in which our industry is, it is even more difficult to talk about salary increases than to talk about salary reductions. (Question) The union has also organized an unemployed group and is prepared to place them with your colleagues in the association. What is your industry's attitude towards this? (Answer) Compulsory placement of unemployed clerks is what this association has always firmly opposed. If the union insists on its own way, a big storm will inevitably follow, and there is no way to avoid it."

Labor Representative's Statement: The standing director of the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union told the reporter of the New Sound News Agency yesterday that Feng Cunren Hall and others have undermined labor-capital conditions and refused outside field substitutes. The union has now decided to issue a warning to the capitalists as the first step according to the resolution. If they do not wake up, the store will be ordered to strike alone. If victory is not achieved, all employees in the city will unite to help. The joint meeting will be held again when the strike is about to begin, and at the same time, the party and government agencies will be reported for assistance. The attitude of the capitalists is tough at the moment, so the strike may become a reality, but we believe that the pharmacy strike is related to local security and has a great impact on the people. We hope that the capitalists will wake up quickly.

Cai Tingkai, commander of the 19th Route Army, went to Guangdong yesterday morning at 4:00 a.m. with Fan Qiwu, the former director of the army's Shanghai office, on the Dollar Line's President Wilson to participate in the mediation of the Guangdong Navy unrest. He is expected to arrive in Hong Kong by noon tomorrow and then transfer to Guangzhou. Fan Shisheng Wounded

Shot Six Times and Admitted to a Hospital in Hankou, National News Agency reports that Fan Shaozeng (Shisheng), the commander of the division currently suppressing bandits in Hubei, attacked the communist bandits in Shashi earlier this month. The fighting was fierce, and Commander Fan took the lead and fought bravely, but he was taken advantage of by the communist bandits and shot six times. His right shoulder blade was broken, but fortunately, none of the wounds were fatal, so his life is not in danger. He had previously invited the Niu Huilin and Niu Huisheng brothers, doctors from Shanghai, and Pang Jingzhou to go for a consultation. The Niu brothers were busy and slightly ill, so they could not leave Shanghai suddenly. Dr. Pang instead arranged for the German doctor Blancus to go. They chartered a plane yesterday morning, preparing to fly to Hankou this morning. They received a telegram from Shashi that Commander Fan had been admitted to a hospital in Hankou, so they stopped. Recently, there has been a rumor in Shanghai that a certain important person was assassinated in Xun and invited Dr. Niu to go for a consultation. It is probably a misrepresentation of this matter.

Li Shijia's Trip to Japan Postponed

Scheduled to go to Japan on the 29th, Japan-Japan News reports that Li Shijia, the standing vice minister of the Navy Department, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing earlier and originally planned to take the Nagasaki Maru to Japan yesterday to discuss the advance delivery of the Ninghai warship. However, due to procedural issues that have not yet been fully negotiated with the Japanese, he was unable to depart and has rescheduled

to go to Japan again on the 29th of this month.

Zhabei Household Survey

The Fifth District Boundary Was Completed Yesterday Morning

Total of 46,047 People

The household survey in the Japanese-withdrawn area has been completed. The final survey forms for the first, second, and third precincts of the Fifth District of Zhabei were distributed to each household on the 21st, requiring them to be filled in and submitted to the bureau within five days. The households filled them out quickly and submitted them all by the afternoon of the 22nd. Yesterday, the Household Registration Section of the Second Division of the Public Security Bureau completed the statistics. There are a total of 25,268 large and small men and 20,779 women in the Chinese resident population in the first, second, and third precincts of the Fifth District, except for the area west of the railway and around Yokohama Bridge, where a small portion of the Japanese army occupied several hundred households and the survey could not be started. As for the foreign residents, they were forwarded by the consuls of various countries and will be submitted on time. There are approximately one thousand households, of which Japanese account for 60% to 70%.

Association for the Care of Fallen Soldiers Welcomes Xiong Xiling

The Association for the Care of the Families of Fallen Soldiers held its third executive and supervisory committee meeting yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM to welcome Mr. Xiong Bing. Those present included Bo Wenwei, Wu Jingxiong, Wang Boyuan, Zhang Shenzhi, Zhu Jiaobo, Xu Shiying, Huang Bodu, Xiong Xiling, Jin Guanfu, Zhu Ziqiao, Cha Liangzhao, Shi Yuemen, Zhang Bo'an, Wu Zhihao, Li Zushen, Huang Hanzhi, Pan Xulun, Pan Gongzhan, Zhang Zhijiang, Weng Guoxun, etc. Xu Jingren was publicly elected as chairman and delivered a speech, saying: "The most important reason for convening today's meeting is to welcome Mr. Tai Bing. Tracing back to the motivation for initiating this association, it was due to the telegram from Xiong Binglao. Recently, Binglao also played a powerful role in the approval of the registration. In the future, we still hope for Binglao's leadership and guidance in the progress of the association." Next, the chairman reported on the letter from the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan and the four points of the Ministry of Interior's proposed amendments to the association's constitution, which were quite appropriate. The association has now responded after correcting them. Next, the proposals were discussed: (1) Wang Boyuan proposed adding a provision to the association's constitution that fallen soldiers in internal wars, except for bandit suppression, should not receive condolences. It was decided to reply that the association has sent a separate letter inviting his family to come to the meeting for a discussion. Finally, Xiong Bing delivered a speech explaining the motivation for initiating the association, the various methods of comforting the families of the deceased, and thanking everyone for their warm welcome. The meeting adjourned around 5:00 PM.

City Chamber of Commerce Commends the Achievements of the Defense Corps

Presenting a Silk Banner

Yesterday's Banner Presentation Ceremony

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, in recognition of the outstanding efforts of the Municipal Defense Corps in assisting the military and police and protecting the local area during the recent Shanghai Incident, specially commissioned a silk banner. Yesterday afternoon, Standing Committee members Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, and Yuan Ludeng led a Boy Scout troop with drums and trumpets to present it to the Defense Corps. The ceremony was held at the public sports ground. All members of the Management Committee, Luo Jingyou, Wen Yingxing, and Yao Mulian, were present, and Luo Jingyou, Yao Mulian, and Wang Binyan were elected as the presidium. Officers of the sixteen district defense corps in the city and all members of the Shanghai South District Corps also attended, numbering several thousand, making it a grand occasion. After the meeting began according to protocol, Wang Xiaolai, chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, delivered a speech, stating that the Municipal Defense Corps had taken on rear area duties during the recent war, working tirelessly day and night. Therefore, although the situation at the time was alarming, with multiple scares in a single night and the future uncertain, the local area was able to maintain stability thanks to the collaborative defense efforts of the Defense Corps, which could not be overlooked. The Chamber of Commerce, on behalf of the city's merchants and residents, presented the silk banner as a memento. He also stated that although the war had come to an end, the difficult times were not over. All citizens must unite and support the government to defend against external aggression and ensure domestic tranquility. Public military force is particularly important, and the Defense Corps is the foundation of public military force. If it can build on this achievement and expand, it will have great hope for the country and the people in the future. After the speech, the banner was presented to Luo Jingyou, chairman of the Management Committee, who accepted the banner and delivered a speech of thanks, stating that the corps was honored to receive such a prestigious banner from the City Chamber of Commerce and that the presence of the leaders of the Chamber of Commerce to offer encouragement was greatly appreciated. He, Luo Jingyou, was honored to be a part of this occasion and, on behalf of the entire corps, accepted the banner with immense pride. The Defense Corps, as the basic military force of the people, aims to assist the military and police, maintain local order, and protect the lives and property of the people. After the January 28th Incident, the war-torn areas were devastated, and even non-war zones experienced frequent scares, with people relocating and fleeing. The direct and indirect losses were significant. Although these devastating losses were due to national survival, the people had no complaints. However, the arrival of the incident was beyond the power of the Defense Corps to resist, but the responsibility could not be shirked. Seeing that the wounds had not yet healed and the scars were still fresh, we received this honorary banner, and in the midst of honor, we could not help but feel infinite sadness and infinite shame. In terms of the service provided by the Defense Corps this time, those in the war zone did their best to assist the police in maintaining local security. The duty of the corps can be somewhat comforting, but strictly speaking, the corps assisted the military in terms of strategy and tactics was still lacking, and the people in the non-war zones were relocating and fleeing, which also showed that the defense force of the corps was not strong and could not gain the trust of the people. This is what the corps should strive to do. Zeng and Hu preserved the country with local militias, and eventually quelled the great chaos, as long as there are methods, and the training is appropriate, achieving the above goals is not difficult. In addition to feeling ashamed, we can only strive to achieve success, so as not to live up to today's grand ceremony. We solemnly express our gratitude.

Lu Tongping, Secretary of the British Embassy in China, Speaks in Shanghai

The British Public Expresses Sympathy for Us. According to New Voice News, Lu Tongping, secretary of the Chinese Embassy in the United Kingdom, arrived in Shanghai yesterday on the British mail ship "Glenogle." A reporter visited him at the Yipinxian Hotel and inquired about the recent situation in the United Kingdom. Mr. Lu answered as follows: Since the September 18th Incident, Ambassador Shi has repeatedly attended the League of Nations Administrative Council meetings in Geneva and Paris, fighting for the country and becoming ill from overwork. Following the doctor's advice, he went to Spain for recuperation at the beginning of the year and returned to London in mid-April. Until I (Mr. Lu speaking of himself) left the United Kingdom in the middle of last month, Shi's health had not fully recovered. In addition to the ambassador, the embassy also has Counselor and Acting Chargé d'Affaires Chen Weicheng, who assists with everything. British public opinion can be divided into two factions. Conservative newspapers such as The Morning Post, Daily Mail, and Daily Telegraph are generally ambiguous and confused, and they inevitably have biased arguments from time to time. Labor newspapers such as the News Chronicle and Daily Herald, and the Manchester Guardian, are able to speak out righteously and without hesitation, expressing considerable sympathy for us. As for the public, their attitude is consistent, and they are extremely dissatisfied with the atrocities of the Japanese. The British intellectual class who support the League of Nations have an organization called the League of Nations Union, with more than one million members and branches all over the country. When the Sino-Japanese incident was serious, they held meetings several times to express their attitude and publish a declaration upholding justice. Its influence on British public opinion and foreign policy is quite large. The current Far Eastern policy of the British diplomatic authorities is also subject to criticism from the union from time to time. Furthermore, during the Shanghai War, a large number of retired British military officers and aviation personnel volunteered to serve in our army, which shows the sympathy of the British public for us. Regarding the League of Nations, because the full report of the investigation team has not yet been completed, it is impossible to carry out important work to mediate the Sino-Japanese incident for a while. Because the League of Nations is not an executive agency, its strength is limited, and the powers are too cautious and unwilling to go all out to support it, so it is difficult to predict the result. Our country's plenipotentiary representatives, Ambassador Shi and Ambassador Yan, are sincere, earnest, and unyielding, and are deeply respected by representatives and public opinion from all countries. The delegation in Geneva now includes Hu Shize, Director of the Office, and Luo Zhongyi, the ambassador to Denmark, in addition to Yan. Wang Jiazhen, the former vice minister of foreign affairs, is also in Geneva as a senior advisor to the delegation.

The Investigation Committee Unseals the Former Anti-Japanese Association Office

The goods seized by the former Anti-Japanese Association, after the municipal government, together with various agencies and groups, formed a joint investigation committee, are being investigated. The former Anti-Japanese Association office has also been temporarily unsealed, and the committee has inspected the goods stored in each warehouse and recorded the situation as follows:

Unsealing the Office: The Shanghai Municipal Government, in response to a request from the Investigation Committee of the Goods Seized by the Former Anti-Japanese Association, temporarily unsealed the former Anti-Japanese Association office. After receiving instructions for approval, it was ordered to handle the matter carefully with the various committee members and report back. The fourth standing meeting of the Investigation Committee also resolved that at 10 a.m. on the 23rd, the various members of the municipal government, the municipal party headquarters, the municipal chamber of commerce, the public security bureau, and the former Anti-Japanese Association would go to the Quanzhe Guild Hall to unseal the former Anti-Japanese Association office in the Tianhou Palace together.

Inspecting the Goods: The various goods seized by the former Anti-Japanese Association have been stored in various warehouses for a long time. The fourth standing meeting of the Investigation Committee resolved that at 10 a.m. on the 24th, the various committees would go to the various warehouses together to inspect them. There were a total of 47 warehouse receipts: 12 from the Continental Bank warehouse, 9 from the Yuanchang warehouse, 7 from the Ningshao warehouse, 2 from the Jiangsu Bank warehouse, 16 from the Dachu warehouse, and 1 from the Dongchang warehouse. After inspection, except for the 50 pieces of foreign cloth originally stored in the Jiangsu Bank warehouse, of which only 26 pieces and 14 bolts remained, the rest were consistent.

Statement from the Certified Public Accountants Association

Shanghai War Losses: Should Be Compensated by Japan

Requesting the Government to Negotiate: Asking for Advance Allocation

The Certified Public Accountants Association declared, "Since the violent Japanese invasion of Songhu on January 28, the rattling of airplanes, the rumbling of heavy artillery, the continuous flames of war, and the devastation everywhere, not only has the land of Qinghua been transformed into a field of rubble, but the tangible losses are countless. Moreover, farmers have stopped plowing, workers have stopped working, merchants have stopped trading, and scholars have abandoned their studies. The intangible losses are even more unknown. Even the wives of widows, the children of orphans, and innocent people have been sacrificed in the ruthless bullets and artillery fire. How many are there? Alas, our people have suffered such great trauma, yet they do not think of seeking compensation for their losses. Is it not a dead heart? Is it enough to destroy the country with the bodies of our 400 million compatriots? If the hearts of our 400 million compatriots die, it will be enough to destroy the country. To avoid the pain of national subjugation, first save the hearts of the dead. If not, let people ravage and destroy as they please, still enduring humiliation and remaining silent. I fear that not only will the powers laugh at our people for being numb and unfeeling, but the enemy will think that our people are willing to endure humiliation, and they may as well make a comeback and show their lewd power again. At that time, there will be no survivors among our people. After the outbreak of the war, this association, in view of the losses suffered by our people, must make a detailed statistics to prepare for demanding compensation from the violent Japanese in the future, that is, to jointly register the losses of the affected people with the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, prepare tables separately, submit them to the central government after review by the members of this association, and seriously negotiate with Japan, demanding full compensation. Unless the goal is achieved, it will never stop. Because this battle was started by Japan, before the Shanghai Incident occurred, Mayor Wu was willing to compromise in order to protect the property of the people of Songhu, and he spared no effort to accept the conditions put forward by the Japanese. Why did he suddenly open fire before the blood was dry? The facts are there, and the nations have seen them. They are wrong and we are right. There is sufficient reason to demand compensation. It is not like climbing a tree to catch a fish. What is worrying is that the diplomacy is weak and the case is delayed, and it cannot be resolved immediately. This association believes that if the government delays and makes mistakes, the people will only have to hold the government accountable and find ways to compensate in advance in the shortest possible time, because Songhu is the Songhu of the entire China. The interests of Songhu on weekdays are shared by the entire country. At this time, the losses of Songhu should also be shared by the entire country. Moreover, the affairs of Songhu this time are the affairs of the entire China and the international community, not the local affairs of China. Since it is the affair of the entire China, the central government should not first find ways to compensate the people of Songhu and let the people of Songhu suffer the losses alone. There is no such reason. Based on this meaning, this association, in addition to asking the central government to seriously negotiate with Japan for compensation for losses, is now making a solemn declaration and hoping that the affected compatriots who have not registered will come to the joint office of the three agencies (located in this association) to register. As the saying goes, 'United, we stand.' Although Japan is violent and tyrannical, if our government argues with reason, our affected compatriots will be able to achieve the final victory." This is the declaration.

Anhui Province Cancels the Special Business Tax

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce appealed to the Ministry of Commerce. Since Anhui Province opened the special business tax, various chambers of commerce believed that it violated the principle of eliminating internal tariffs. Moreover, after the natural disasters and wars, the vitality has not recovered, the commerce has been declining, and they cannot afford it. They have requested the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce to forward the request for cancellation. The association, based on the situation, sent telegrams to the central government, and yesterday received an order from the Ministry of Finance, which has been forwarded to cancel it. Now, the Ministry of Finance's telegram to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce is recorded: (Title omitted) The telegram from Jiang has been received. After checking the case of Anhui Province collecting special business tax, the letter from the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan was approved. The President ordered that the cancellation be forwarded immediately. It has been consulted and ordered by the province to comply with the original plan of the Executive Yuan. Hereby, a telegram is sent to inform you.

Various Trade Associations Oppose the Special Business Tax

Since the Central Government has Already Cancelled it, Why Allow the Merchants and the People to Suffer Again? The local Timber Industry Association, Timber Trade Association, Flower Trade Association, Bamboo Trade Association, Paper Trade Association, Sand Boat Trade Association, Pig Trade Association, etc., jointly sent a letter to the City Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating, "Dear Sirs, the Jiangsu Provincial Government plans to implement a special business tax that is a disguised form of internal tariffs, which is harmful to merchants and the people. After repeated appeals from various industries, fortunately, the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Commerce approved the cancellation. However, news has spread that the Jiangsu Provincial Government is disregarding the central government's cancellation order and is determined to implement the collection from July 1st and has set up a general office in Shanghai. It is extremely shocking. Merchants and the people are unable to bear this harsh tax after the disaster. Needless to say, in terms of the political system, the Jiangsu Provincial Government is still a national official appointed by the central government and should obey the central government. Now it is disregarding the orders of the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Commerce. For the harsh tax that the central government has approved for cancellation in order to show compassion for the people's suffering, it must be implemented, as if it has already broken away from the central government and is determined to oppress our people again. Merchants, etc., belong to the same country and are greatly puzzled by this kind of transgressive decree. Even if they are able to obey, there are still doubts. Moreover, they are unable to afford it, so how can they sit still and wait for their own demise? Your association is a commercial guarantee, and you must have a strong method to save the situation at this critical moment of life and death. Our association is deeply afflicted and cannot remain silent. We respectfully request that you send a telegram to the central government to stop it immediately. If the Jiangsu Provincial Government refuses to comply with the central government, how will it be handled? Whether our people obey the central government or belong to the provincial government, please give instructions. We beg for your assessment and implementation. We will be grateful."

From July 1st, the Jianghai Customs Will Collect a Unified Tax on Rice and Wheat

Collecting National Currency One Dime Per Package. The Jianghai Customs issued a notice regarding the collection of a unified tax on imported wheat flour, stating, "For the purpose of the notice, it is found that the Jianghai Customs has been collecting a unified tax on wheat flour and other goods since May 16, 1931, as recorded in Notice No. 1212 on May 11 of that year. From July 1 of this year, all imported wheat flour will be taxed at a rate of one dime of national currency per package according to the unified tax rate. The weight should be based on 49 pounds as the standard. If the original package is less than 49 pounds, it will also be taxed as one package. If it exceeds 49 pounds, it will be calculated proportionally. All merchants are hereby informed. This notice is hereby given. June 24, 21st year of the Republic of China, Customs Officer Luo Fude."

Wu Shifang, the district chief of Minhang Town in the county, in view of the prevalence of cholera in various places and the dense population in this district, and because this year is after the Shanghai War, it is expected that the epidemic will be more severe than in the past. Two Civilian Residences in Zhabei Were Destroyed During the War

The Municipal Government allocated funds to repair the First and Third Civilian Residences in Zhabei. Because they were located in the war zone, they were severely damaged. Recently, civilians from the disaster area have returned one after another, and the civilian residences urgently need to be rebuilt. Wu Xingya, Director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and Shen Yi, Director of the Municipal Public Works Bureau, specially submitted a request to the Municipal Government to allocate funds for the reconstruction. The original submission is recorded as follows:

Original Submission from the Two Bureaus: Regarding the fact that the First and Third Civilian Residences have been damaged due to the war and urgently need to be repaired, a joint document is respectfully submitted for your assessment and instructions. It is respectfully noted that during the anti-Japanese war, the First Civilian Residence on Quanjia'an Road and the Third Civilian Residence on Jiaotong Road were both located within the war zone and could not be managed. After the Japanese soldiers withdrew, the bureaus sent personnel to investigate. The damage to the First Civilian Residence was relatively small, but the Third Civilian Residence was severely damaged by artillery fire. It is estimated that eight rooms, including No. 81, were completely destroyed, and four rooms, including No. 141, were half-destroyed. The roofs, walls, doors, and windows of the remaining houses were pierced by bullet holes, and the damage varied. The original water and electricity facilities of the two residences were mostly lost due to lack of management. Now that the situation is gradually stabilizing and residents are moving back one after another, repairs should be carried out as soon as possible to ensure residence. Regarding the costs of repairs, the Public Works Bureau has carefully estimated that a total of 3,500 yuan will be required, including the repair of the auditorium and bamboo fences of the First Residence. Because the project is trivial and not suitable for bidding, it is proposed that Wang Runji, the original contractor of the Third Civilian Residence, be ordered to carry out the repairs within a specified period. In addition to the costs of repairing and supplementing water and electricity facilities, which have been submitted by the Social Affairs Bureau in another case, the reasons for repairing the damaged parts of the First and Third Civilian Residences due to the war are whether or not they are appropriate. It is appropriate to submit the estimated price list, jointly submit it for your assessment, and if you approve it, please order the Finance Bureau to allocate the aforementioned expenditures in full so that it can be carried out. It will be convenient for the public. Respectfully submitted to Mayor Wu, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Wu Xingya, and Director of the Public Works Bureau Shen Yi.

Approval from the Municipal Government: After receiving the submission, Mayor Wu of the Municipal Government immediately approved it and immediately ordered the Finance Bureau to allocate funds for construction. The original approval is recorded as follows: The submitted list has been read in full. The repair expenses for the two residences are approved to be allocated 3,000 yuan. The municipal treasury is now in deficit, so it is essential to strictly economize expenditures. This is of utmost importance. In addition to ordering the Finance Bureau, you should comply with this order.

Elementary School Students Enlist in the Army

Willing to Expel the Japanese Rampaging in Eastern Provinces. Wu Moqing, a sixteen-year-old student at the Shisi Voluntary Elementary School on Pingliang Road in Pudong, is from Ningbo, Zhejiang Province, and currently lives in Lane 2, Changanli, Yangshupu Road. He has been studying at the school for six years and is expected to graduate this summer. His grades and conduct at school have been good. Unexpectedly, he left a letter and ran away to enlist in the army (on the morning of the 23rd). His friend Yu Chongchun (age 16) went with him. Yu was Wu's classmate in the same grade, but Yu dropped out of school last winter because his family lacked manpower to manage the store (a small tobacco and paper store). The two students usually traveled and went together, and they had similar interests, so they agreed to go together this time. It is said that the families of the two students are now extremely anxious and have asked people to look for them everywhere. The letter is attached below:

Dear Mother, I am not going for anything else. I have endured the anger in my belly for nearly a year. Since the Japanese invaded the three northeastern provinces on September 18 last year, Chinese military and political leaders have not sent a single soldier, only knowing how to retreat and unwilling to resist. Fortunately, some smart people in the three provinces have organized groups to fight the Japanese invaders. It is truly admirable and commendable. Seeing this situation, I should have gone to defend the country long ago, but we are young and could not find a place to enlist in the army for a while. After spending a lot of effort, I finally learned where to enlist in the army. If I go to serve as a soldier, I will definitely contribute to the country, preserve the motherland, and drive the Japanese rampant in the three northeastern provinces. If I sacrifice my life, I will die with a clear conscience. After I leave, please do not grieve, because every commoner has a responsibility for the rise and fall of the country, so I am going to contribute to the country. I care for the country, so I cannot care for the family, so please do not miss me.

Local Court Plans to Establish a Higher Court

To Hear Second Instance Cases Under Its Jurisdiction. The Ministry of Justice and Administration stated that the jurisdiction of the higher courts in various places is vast, the establishment of branches is incomplete, and even minor cases in remote areas must be appealed to the higher court far away, which is inconvenient in terms of both time and economy. Therefore, it is proposed that before the promulgation of the Court Organization Law, higher courts should be temporarily established in the local courts under the jurisdiction of the higher courts of various provinces to hear civil second instance cases under the jurisdiction of the local courts nearby. The local court in this city has been ordered to prepare for it.

Zhabei Shantytown: Over 30,000 Households Targeted for Municipal Government Removal Plan

The number of poor migrants from other provinces residing in Zhabei is substantial. These people live together in family groups and arbitrarily build shantytowns in deserted and remote areas. This not only spoils the appearance of the city but also provides a haven for bandits and thieves. During the recent Shanghai battle, these poor people were even exploited by the Japanese. In light of this, the municipal government, taking advantage of the relatively stable situation, has issued an order to various municipal bureaus to carefully plan measures for removing the Zhabei shantytowns. The plan will proceed in two stages: first, to find ways to concentrate the shantytown residents, and second, to build as many affordable housing units as possible.

Liuying Road and other areas have been designated as shantytown concentration zones. The municipal government has already approved this plan, but because the Liuying area has already been designated for the establishment of the Third Public Sports Ground, instructions have been issued to re-examine appropriate locations. The original submissions from the various bureaus and the municipal government's instructions are recorded below:

Removal Plan – Order Instructing Various Municipal Bureaus to Confer and Decide on Measures for Removing Zhabei Shantytowns. The original submission stated: "Submission Regarding the Formulation of Post-War Shantytown Removal Measures, Jointly Submitted for Review and Approval. Upon investigation, the city's shantytowns, according to a survey conducted by the Municipal Police Bureau in December of last year, number 30,573 households, scattered throughout the urban area, significantly impacting social order and public health. Previously, we received an order from Your Excellency to approve the removal of newly built shantytowns while simultaneously constructing affordable housing units to gradually accommodate the residents. Over the past three years, more than 800 affordable housing units have been built, but the large number of shantytown residents makes it difficult to accommodate them all. Even with continued expansion, it is impossible to achieve immediate results and meet today's urgent needs. Since the recent Anti-Japanese War, the filth and squalor of the shantytowns have become even more apparent. After inspecting the Zhabei districts after the war, new shantytowns have sprung up one after another. Learning from the past and preventing future occurrences, it is truly necessary to remove them. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, on June 4th, convened a meeting with this bureau and others to discuss post-war removal measures. It was unanimously agreed that for the sake of social order, hygiene, city appearance, and urban reconstruction, thorough removal is essential. However, considering the economic hardship after the war and sympathizing with the shantytown residents, it seems appropriate to modify the original removal measures. It was decided that when affordable housing units cannot fully accommodate the residents, the principle of concentrating shantytowns should be adopted. The city's shantytowns will be removed in stages by district. The area south of the Public Concession and the Beijing-Shanghai Railway will be the first district, and the area north of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and south of Zhongxing Road will be the second district. After successful implementation, the remaining two districts will be addressed. The first district currently has approximately 3,000 households, with the exact number to be determined by the Municipal Police Bureau's district investigation. This area is closest to the city center and most affected by municipal facilities. It is proposed to relocate the existing shantytowns. Furthermore, as the shantytown residents are mostly poor, while many are unruly, some are undoubtedly good people. Considering the circumstances and reason, it seems appropriate to provide relocation assistance when relocating them. It is proposed to provide each household with one yuan, requiring approximately 10,000 yuan for the first district. It is requested that Your Municipal Government allocate these funds to facilitate the project. In the future, after concentration, small ditches will be dug around the perimeter to delineate the boundaries. The construction of shantytowns within the perimeter should be regulated in rows to facilitate management and reduce the risk of fire. These matters will be handled by the Municipal Works Bureau. Internal security, supervision, and hygiene matters will be handled separately by the Municipal Police Bureau and the Health Branch Bureau. Respectfully submitted to Mayor Wu, Finance Bureau Director Cai Zengji, Works Bureau Director Shen Yi, Police Bureau Director Wen Yingsing, Land Bureau Director Jin Xingren, and Health Bureau Director Hu Hongji. Social Affairs Bureau Ya."

Municipal Government Instructions – After receiving the submission, the Municipal Government immediately approved it. Regarding the address issue, because Liuying Road has already been designated for the establishment of the Third Public Sports Ground, instructions have been issued to re-examine appropriate locations. The instructions stated: "The joint submission has been reviewed. The proposed removal measures are feasible. However, the Liuying Road Xin Yingpan address was previously requested by the Education Bureau for use as the Third Sports Ground and has been approved by this city and communicated to the Ministry of Military Affairs. Regarding the address for concentrating the shantytowns, the said bureau and others are instructed to confer and select another location for submission and inspection. This order."

Both Bandit and Victim are Key Suspects in Murder Case

Police have conducted a detailed investigation.

Scene of the murder re-enacted.

All defendants steadfastly denied allegations yesterday.

Magistrate advocated for further detailed investigation.

Kong Guangfu, a native of Anhui residing at 746 Yongji Lane, Weihaiwei Road, reported to the Xinzha Police Station at 8 p.m. on the 16th of this month, claiming that his home had been burglarized and robbed of 580 yuan in property. He stated that he recognized two of the thieves, brothers named Zhou Zhongyi and Zhou Zhonghua. Upon receiving the report, the police station ordered Chinese Detective Tang Jian, Detective Hua Youshan, and Western Detective Ke Ying, among others, to proceed to 3923 Daxu Lane, Laobeisheng Road, to arrest the Zhou brothers. However, the Zhou brothers vehemently denied the robbery and claimed that Kong was involved in

The Murder of Wang Abao. Not long after, Zhang Guomin, a friend of Kong, went to the police station to visit him and was also accused by the Zhou brothers of being Kong's accomplice. The police chief ordered that Kong, Zhang, and the Zhou brothers be detained. On the morning of the 18th, they were sent to the First Special District Court. The police charged the Zhou brothers with robbery, but because the police had not investigated the murder case involving Kong and Zhang, they requested permission to detain them. The court ordered that Kong and Zhang be detained, and the Zhou brothers be held for further questioning at a later date. This information has been reported in this newspaper. Now, the Chinese and Western detectives handling this case have, during the extended period, conducted a

Detailed Investigation and have discovered that Kong, Zhang, and the Zhou brothers are all key suspects in the murder case. Kong served as the commander, Zhang as his deputy, and the Zhou brothers as accomplices. In 1929, all four defendants were officials in the municipal party headquarters, and the Zhou brothers were also foremen at the Japanese-owned Dongya Coir Bag Factory on Laobeisheng Road in western Shanghai. At that time, there was a surge in labor strikes at various factories. Kong and others

Organized a Union in secret and directed the strikes. They then sent Zhou Zhongyi (nicknamed "Little Slippery") and Zhou Zhonghua (nicknamed "Big Slippery") to the home of Wang Abao (also known as Xie Abao) at 2252 Nanfu Lane, Laobeisheng Road (Wang was also a foreman at the coir bag factory), to persuade Wang to join the union and incite workers to strike. Because Wang refused, the union offered a reward of 1,000 yuan to murder Wang Abao. On the morning of December 12, 1929, at 5:30 a.m., Wang was

Shot Dead near his residence in Nanfu Lane and collapsed next to a water tap. After the incident, Kong received a reward of 200 yuan, Zhang received 80 yuan, and the Zhou brothers each received 40 yuan. After Wang's murder, the Putuo Road Police Station, which had jurisdiction at the time, paid close attention and sent detectives to investigate secretly. Because the Zhou brothers were suspected of involvement in the murder, they were detained by the police. However, due to insufficient evidence, they were released. This time, after the police conducted a new investigation, it was suspected that the four defendants were indeed involved in the murder of Zhu Abao.

And it's Not Just This Case. They are also suspected of being involved in the murder of Tan Yisheng, Dong Qigui, Shi Jingui, and several other cases. Therefore, each defendant was ordered to write a confession. Several days prior, Kong Guangfu was ordered to accompany detectives to the scene to re-enact the murder, and the spot where the victim collapsed. The remaining three defendants were also brought to the scene to re-enact the events, which were consistent with the

Police's Investigation at the time of the incident. Yesterday morning, at 8:30 a.m., the police escorted the four defendants to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang detailed the above situation and stated that the four defendants were being prosecuted under Article 284, Paragraph 1, of the Criminal Code for the murder of Xie Abao (aka Wang Abao) on December 12, 1929, at 5:30 a.m. on Laobeisheng Road, Nanfu Lane.

Regarding Other Murder Cases, the police have not yet completed their investigation and will not prosecute them at this time. The confessions were submitted to the court for investigation. The defendants were defended by lawyers Fan Gang, Li Shirui, and Zhu Honglie, who had been hired. Subsequently, Xie Wangshi, the mother of the victim Xie Abao, and Sun Xieshi, his sister, filed statements proving everything. When questioned, Zhou Zhongyi testified, "I know nothing about Wang Abao's murder. I accused Kong Guangfu of robbery because he falsely accused me of being a thief."

"Actually, Wang Abao was killed by the Communist Party. At that time, I was an official in the municipal party headquarters and did not interfere. Even if Wang had done something illegal, I could have reported it to the judicial authorities or the Social Affairs Bureau for punishment. It had nothing to do with me. Moreover, Wang was a good friend of mine from the same factory, and I knew his mother and sister. I could never

Do anything illegal. Please investigate." Zhou Zhonghua testified, "I did not go to Wang's home to urge him to join the union or incite a strike. Kong falsely accused the police. Therefore, I also accused him of murder. The 40 yuan was not a reward; it was a loan from Kong." Kong Guangfu testified that from 1927 to 1929, he was an official in the municipal party headquarters. Presiding Magistrate Wu Tingqi asked him if the deceased, Wang Abao, was a foreman at the coir bag factory and that he had ordered him to strike but failed. So, he had him beaten to death with a reward of 1,000 yuan,

"You got 200 yuan. Zhang Guomin got 80 yuan. The Zhou brothers each got 40 yuan. Did this happen?" Kong replied, "No. The incident was because I had a quarrel with Zhou Zhonghua last year over debt collection, which led to a fight. We both went to the headquarters, so we had a grudge. I am now being falsely accused. The confession at the police station was given involuntarily and untruthfully." Zhang Guomin also testified that he was an official in the municipal party headquarters and denied being the deputy commander or murdering Wang Abao. After verifying the confessions, Magistrate Wu stated that the

Case still required further investigation and ordered the four defendants to be remanded in custody for further questioning on the morning of July 2nd.

Suspicious Hanging Corpse

Four feet off the ground.

Blood on forehead and flower in the ear.

Residents of Donggou Town gossip.

Planned murder?

A man was found hanging from a tree in the wasteland along the Donggou River in Pudong. The situation was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Wang Chongshan, the chief of the Third District's Fifth Precinct, investigated and found that the residents of the town said the deceased was a worker at the Donggou Match Factory and was from Shaoxing. A Mr. Lu stated that he was returning home late at night with a lantern and saw three people talking. One said, "This person is really honest; don't harm him." Another said, "He must die." Lu shone the lantern on them and was punched. Lu fled in terror. It was also found that the deceased was four feet off the ground, there were drops of blood on his forehead, and a pearl flower was in his right ear. All of these facts were strange. An inquiry was made with the match factory, but they denied having such an employee. It became a suspicious case. For a time, the residents of Donggou Town were in an uproar. Until yesterday, when prosecutors from the local court arrived and verified that the deceased had indeed hanged himself. The bloodstains on his forehead appeared to be caused by a hole the size of a bean, as if he had climbed the tree and been poked by a branch. The flower was replaced with a piece of white paper. The bailiff collected the body and took photos, waiting for someone to claim it. However, the elderly residents of the town said that this was a planned murder, meaning that the talk led to the hanging. No matter what, it will be verified as a suicide by hanging to avoid criminal liability unless the perpetrators are caught, in which case the truth can be revealed.

Customs' Hai Xing Patrol Ship to be Launched on Schedule

In light of the recent rampant piracy and the fear of merchants and travelers, the Shanghai Jianghai Customs entrusted the Jiangnan Shipyard with the construction of two patrol ships, named Hua Xing and Hai Xing, to strengthen the police force.
