Public Security and Health Bureaus Pay Attention to Citizens' Summer Health

Jointly issue a ban on the sale of unsanitary food and drinks. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security and Health Bureaus have jointly issued a proclamation regarding the ban on the sale of unsanitary food and drinks: "Proclamation: It has been found that the summer season is approaching and epidemics are prone to occur. All raw water and naturally-made ice, ice cream, shaved ice, sour plum soup, Dutch water jelly, and other foods and drinks are media for spreading disease. In order to prevent the breeding of epidemics and protect the health of citizens, the bureaus are strictly prohibiting the sale of all of the aforementioned unsanitary foods and drinks. All kinds of food and drinks sold in stalls, as well as cut fruits, must be covered with gauze. Otherwise, business is prohibited. If not complied with, severe punishment will be inflicted upon discovery. This proclamation is hereby issued."

Rice Industry Asks for Delay in Adopting New Hu

Changing the rice hu

Increases the burden.

The Shanghai rice industry has been using the Hai hu as the standard for selling rice. The difference between the Social Affairs Bureau's new hu and the Hai hu is 1.6 dou per shi (8.4 dou). But the Social Affairs Bureau has ordered the Bean and Rice Industry Association to switch to the new hu starting July 1st and notify the industry to comply. The North-South Rice Industry Association held a meeting and unanimously agreed that implementing the new hu would increase the burden on consumers. They have petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau to temporarily postpone the implementation. Various labor groups have learned of this and sent representatives to the leaders of the rice industry in the past two days, requesting that they not use the new hu. The leaders responded that they had already pleaded with the Social Affairs Bureau to be mindful of the difficulties of merchants and the people and to postpone the change.

Case of Unauthorized Removal of Li Jishen's Home Electronics

Heard once yesterday.

The intent is unclear.

Zhang Zhijie, a local resident, aged 18, along with Huang Axiang, Huang Minggao, Zhao Fugui, Ping Ade, and two others, hired two cars, numbers 08605 and 18242, on the afternoon of the 14th of this month. They trespassed into the residence of Central Committee Member Li Jishen at 3 Lane 163, Luban Road, in the French Concession, removed the installed wireless electronics, loaded them onto the cars, and hid them at Zhao Fugui's place on Jisi Fei'er Road. Before leaving, they made an appointment with Li's family to discuss the matter, hoping to extort money. The victim reported the matter to the police. Jin Jiulin, a detective inspector of the special organ, discovered that Zhang and others were hiding in Room 402 of the Oriental Hotel on Xizang Road. He, along with head detective Li Yaolong, deputy detective Qian Yumin, Zhang Ziying, and patrol detectives, went to the Oriental Hotel and arrested Zhang and the other five people, recovered the stolen goods, and brought them back to the police station, and sent them to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and investigation. Yesterday morning, Magistrate Li Changnian, along with clerk Wu Shan, came to the First Criminal Court to continue the hearing. Police lawyer Gu Shouxi first stated the facts of the case and prosecuted under Article 33

8, Paragraph 4 of the Criminal Law. Zhang Jie, on behalf of the plaintiff, stated the circumstances of the defendant's removal of the machine and requested the court to question the defendants about their backgrounds. Witness Lu Qinliang stated that he was a communications officer at Li's residence. On that day, I went to Li's residence at 2 p.m. to take over the shift and saw that the defendants had removed the machine. I asked them why they were removing it. The first defendant replied that it was illegal and carried it onto the car. Zhang Zhijie testified that Chen Guisheng had instructed him to move it. It was said that the purchase price had not been paid, so I asked Huang Minggao to invite the other defendants to remove it and store it at Zhao Fugui's place. They returned to the Oriental Hotel to wait for Chen Guisheng, who never showed up. The case was then investigated. Huang Axiang testified that he worked for Huang Minggao and that his master ordered him to go. Huang Minggao testified that he was a doctor. Zhang came to see him for medical treatment that day and asked me to find someone to move it. I asked Huang, Zhao, and Ping to go together. Zhang cut the wires and moved it. I didn't know that they were going to move the electronics. Zhao and Ping testified that they were friends with Huang Minggao and that Huang had asked them to go. The plaintiff's representative also stated that the machine was not purchased in Shanghai. It was moved from the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing and installed in Shanghai. Defendant One was defended by lawyer Wang Shizong. Magistrate Li verified the confession and ordered that the hearing be adjourned for further investigation. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Residents of Zhabei Youyu Lane Oppose Landlord's Forced Registration

All the tenants of Youyu Lane on Zhabei Gonghe Road moved out during the Shanghai Incident. They only returned on May 16, when the Japanese troops withdrew. It has only been a month since then. The landlord, Fuyu Company, disregarding the tenants' difficulties, hired lawyer Chen Jinrong to issue proclamations stating that the landlord would voluntarily waive two, three, or four months of rent, provided that everyone registered and paid all outstanding rent at the same time. Otherwise, it would be considered a cancellation of the lease. The tenants of the lane, due to the evacuation, had no money to pay the outstanding rent and were long-time tenants, so it seemed unnecessary to register. Therefore, they did not register or pay the outstanding rent. On the 6th of this month, the landlord threatened that the houses would be renovated and ordered everyone to move out within the month. The tenants of the lane sent four representatives to Fuyu Company, the landlord, on Mengdelan Road, to petition manager Yu Jingfu, asking him to sympathize with the people's difficulties, cancel the renovation and demand for outstanding rent, and reduce the rent. However, the manager not only refused their request but also proposed three conditions: (1) The tenants must pay for the drawing fees (approximately 300 yuan). (2) The rent for May and June must be paid by the end of this month, along with one-third of the outstanding rent. (3) In July and August, in addition to paying the original rent, the outstanding rent must be paid in full. If they did not agree, the houses would be renovated. The representatives believed that the manager was obviously threatening them and obstructing them, so yesterday afternoon, they sent two representatives to the Municipal Rent Reduction Association to request assistance and to apply to join the association as members. After the Rent Reduction Association made detailed inquiries, it seemed that the landlord was oppressing them, so it agreed to their request and submitted it to the association's discussion yesterday and the special meeting of the delegates' meeting today for discussion. They will then submit it to today's delegates' meeting for a decision, providing as much assistance as possible.

Special News from the Shipping Industry

Naval ship worker falls into the water. The Jianghai Customs patrol ship Hai Xing was patrolling outside Wusong this time and returned to Shanghai, docking at the Lujiazui Wharf to unload cargo. It was Thursday morning at 9:00 a.m. Worker He Chun was working on the ship when the hoisting rope broke and He Chun fell into the river. The crew of the Hai Xing tried to recover the body but failed. As of yesterday, it had not been found and was presumed drowned. The ship has reported to the customs for compensation.

News of a Riverboat Encounter. Yesterday, the Shanghai shipping industry reported that the Sanbei Company's Yangtze River boat Songpu was transferred to Nanjing by the Ministry of Military Affairs the day before to transport bandit suppression troops to Jiujiang, Hankou, etc. Yesterday, news came that the Songpu boat had run aground en route due to the river level falling. It is now being towed and will be able to leave the shallows when the tide rises. Inquiries to the company did not yield detailed reports. Also, the company's Xing Shi boat was attacked by bandits downstream of Shashi. The troops stationed on the boat resisted but were no match. As a result, hundreds of bags of salt were looted and one passenger was killed. The ship has now arrived in Shashi.

Upstream sends ship to protect navigation. The upper reaches of the Yangtze River, in the Chenglinji area, are entirely bandit strongholds. Merchant ships passing through the area are often robbed. Merchant ships now fly foreign merchant flags. The Second Team of the Yangtze River Navy has also sent ships from Hankou to the upper reaches of Yuezhou Chenglinji to provide escort.

Verdict in the Case of Tong Tai Yong against the Insurance Company

19th Route Army Denies Guerrilla Warfare. Tong Tai Yong, a canned food store on Xihuaide Road in Hongkou, was suddenly engulfed in flames on February 2, during the height of the Sino-Japanese war. The store had insured its fire insurance for 10,000 taels of silver with the Hequn Business Company, so it immediately sought compensation. Hequn initially claimed that they were only an agency and that the insurance was underwritten by the German company Selexia, and that they should negotiate with that company. Chen Lianghuai, the manager of Tong Tai Yong, argued that Hequn had not made this statement at the time of the guarantee, which was a pretext to evade liability. He hired lawyer Lin Jieqing to sue the First Special District Court. Hequn also hired lawyer Shen Yuesheng to defend the suit. In addition to pointing out that the subject of the lawsuit was wrong and that they should negotiate with Selexia's Shanghai agent, they also based their defense on a letter from the Japanese Consulate, stating that Chinese guerrillas had attacked Japanese troops at that time and place, so Japanese soldiers had opened fire in retaliation, causing the store to catch fire and be destroyed. In this case, the plaintiff's insurance was not for war risks, so they were not liable for compensation. In order to clarify the cause of the fire, the plaintiff's lawyer sent a letter to the headquarters of the 19th Route Army to investigate the battle situation on that day.

Page 16

The Army Headquarters replied, stating, in brief: "We have received a letter stating that Tong Tai Yong canned food store was suddenly burned down on February 2 of this year, resulting in tens of thousands of taels of silver in damages. However, according to the Japanese Consul in Shanghai, Chinese guerrillas fired on Japanese troops in the area on that day. Please provide detailed information to provide a basis for our investigation. It has been verified that the 19th Route Army did not have any guerrilla units during the anti-Japanese war in Shanghai. The statements made by the Japanese Consul are obviously fictitious and intended to evade responsibility. We have replied to the letter and hope that you will investigate and negotiate truthfully." Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao held a continued hearing on the case. Lawyer Lin presented the above letter as evidence. Then, Westerner Polayi of the Fire Brigade was called to testify about the firefighting process. He stated that the fire trucks stopped at the intersection of Wuchang Road and Miller Road, 20 to 30 yards from the fire. At the time, a Japanese officer said that Chinese guerrillas were firing from the roof of Tong Tai Yong, and the witness heard gunshots and saw bullet casings on the ground nearby. But it was impossible to determine whether the store was destroyed by guerrillas or by Japanese troops firing on guerrillas. Ge Ge, a fire expert at the Sanyi Foreign Company, testified that he was hired by Hequn Company to assess the damage after the incident. At that time, the Japanese troops had not withdrawn, and they said that the fire was caused by fighting with guerrillas. But he estimated the actual loss of the store to be about 3,900 taels of silver and discussed with Mr. Zheng that such fire losses were difficult for the insurer to bear. Subsequently, the lawyers for both parties debated and concluded the case. The judge ordered a recess and will announce the verdict at a later date.

Yao Zhujiao Road Morphine Apparatus Case Verdict

Zhao and Ou Sentenced to Three Years

Plus a Fine of Five Thousand Yuan

At No. 121 Yao Zhujiao Road, French Concession, on the third floor of a Western-style house, someone had privately set up a morphine drug manufacturing apparatus. This was discovered by detectives Lu Jinbao and Cao Fuchang of the Beidang Road Police Station. They reported to Western Inspector Lü Aicai (transliteration), who led a team of officers to search the premises around 2:00 AM on the 12th of this month. They seized two motorized machines and a large number of accessories, such as glass containers and rubber equipment, along with over 190 catties of finished and unfinished wet and dry raw drug powders. Five people were arrested on the spot: Hou Yunshan and Hou Liru, father and son from Guizhou; and Liu Mingzhang, Tu Hongfa, and Jin Yushan, cooks and laborers from Sichuan and Hubei. All five were taken to the police station for investigation. The next morning at 11:00 AM, Zhao Youming (previously mistakenly identified as being from Sichuan), residing at No. 448 Malang Road, and Ou Yongxiang, residing at No. 4, Lane 169, Lüban Road, both from Sichuan, went to the French General Police Station to see Western Inspector Sa Cai'er (transliteration). Zhao claimed that he had rented the house and sublet it to Wang Hanzhang, who had privately set up the manufacturing of prohibited items. He wanted to intervene to avoid prosecution and secure the release of the detainees. After the Western Inspector reported to the General Inspector, Zhao and Ou were detained and sent to the Second Special District Court for prosecution under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law. Judge Xiong Huiping presided over the trial. The defendants hired lawyers Xu Yannian and Zhao Zuwei to defend them. After the trial, a verdict date was set. Subsequently, the trial judge discovered that the case also involved a car registered under Zhao Youming's name, and that the third defendant, Hou Yunshan, had acted as a bookkeeper, among other suspicious circumstances. Therefore, a retrial was specifically ordered. The retrial took place on the afternoon of the 23rd, focusing on the suspicious points. After the retrial, the debate was declared closed, and the case was submitted for judgment. Yesterday, the verdict was announced. The defendants' lawyers arrived at the court successively after 2:00 PM to await the judgment. At 3:30 PM, Judge Xiong, accompanied by clerk Tao Zongkan, took their seats in the first criminal court and ordered the defendants to be brought to court. After briefly questioning their ages, origins, and occupations, the verdict was announced. The main points were: Zhao Youming (also known as Pi Cheng and Hong Qing) and Ou Shuixiang (also known as Xi Cheng) were each sentenced to three years imprisonment and fined fifty yuan for the crime of jointly manufacturing opium substitutes. Hou Yunshan was sentenced to one year imprisonment and fined four thousand yuan for the crime of directly and significantly assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes. Liu Mingzhang, Hou Lihe, Tu Hongfa, and Jin Yushan were each sentenced to one year imprisonment and fined two thousand four hundred yuan for the crime of assisting in the manufacture of opium substitutes. If the fines were converted to imprisonment, the total amount would be calculated proportionally to the number of days in a year. The number of days in pretrial detention would be credited at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Zhao's defense lawyer, Xu Yannian, requested that the defendant be allowed bail during the appeal period to find the main offender, Wang Hanzhang, and bring him to justice. Ou's defense lawyer, Zhao Zuwei, also requested that his client be granted bail during the appeal period to await instructions. The court also ordered Zhao Youming and Ou Yongxiang to each pay a bail of 50,000 yuan during the appeal period to suspend their detention.

Defendant Not Guilty: Plaintiff Sentenced to Imprisonment

Zhen Tai Dyeing Shop on Mindeli Road, Hanjian Bridge, Zhabei, was jointly established by Li Shande and others. The lawyers on both sides debated fiercely. Yesterday, the court announced its verdict. The main points were: defendant Li Shande was found not guilty. Coveting a Young Woman, Giving Money for Treatment

Causing Marital Disputes Li Yaogen, a native of Zhenjiang, who lives at No. 128 Kongjia Lane, owns a western goods shop. He has a single daughter named Meilan, who is twenty years old. She had been betrothed to a Gao family, but the marriage was dissolved because the Gao son was not engaged in proper business. Unexpectedly, Meilan became ill with resentment. Her father had lost his job and lacked money for treatment. A neighbor, Ren Shouting, a forty-six-year-old from Henan, who already has a wife and two concubines, saw that Meilan was beautiful and had the idea of pursuing her. Knowing that Meilan was sick, he asked a tailor to bring 100 yuan to Li Yaogen to pay for his daughter's treatment. Li was afraid to accept it, but the tailor said that this was a charitable act by the great philanthropist Ren Shouting and did not need to be repaid. When Meilan recovered, Ren Shouting came to visit and eventually talked about marriage, wanting to marry Meilan as his wife. The tailor exaggerated Ren's wealth, claiming that he was a rich man. However, Meilan knew that Ren already had three wives and refused to marry him, politely declining. She was later betrothed to a Feng family and has already married. Unexpectedly, Ren Shouting secretly instructed Meilan to go to the Feng family a month ago, accusing Meilan of breach of promise and fraudulently obtaining money, demanding the return of the loan and engagement money totaling 3,000 yuan. Feng brought Ren to the Laozha Police Station for investigation. After questioning, the police chief determined that the case was related to marriage and instructed them to file a lawsuit in court. Unexpectedly, at 6:00 PM yesterday, Ren Shouting went to Li Yaogen's house to argue. Police officer Peng Yifeng brought Li and Ren to the First Branch of the Second District. After questioning, Director Xu recorded Ren Shouting's statement that he had engaged the defendant's daughter Meilan through a matchmaker in January of last year, but the defendant had secretly betrothed his daughter to someone else, committing fraud. Li Yaogen and his wife, Ruan, stated that the plaintiff was attempting to induce marriage, falsely claiming to donate money for treatment and claiming to be charitable, but in reality, he was coveting their daughter. The so-called engagement was without their daughter's consent, and their daughter had already expressed her unwillingness and was freely betrothed to a Feng family. The court ordered that they be sent to the General Bureau for further investigation.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Literature and Art

Lamenting Wusong in the Rain

— Cha Yiqing

I have been serving at the Wusong Coast Radio Station. Since escaping from the January 28th Incident, I have been staying in the concession for over four months. Yesterday, I went with a friend to lament Wusong. It happened to be during the continuous plum rain. The desolation filled the eyes. The radio station that once stood straight into the clouds had been bombed and destroyed. Tracing the battle, I couldn't help but feel moved. So I wrote four quatrains to share with the readers. The flames of war opened without warning, leaving only the sorrow of burnt gardens. On the misty, plum-rainy Wusong Road, the towering radio station is no longer seen. The winding path is desolate and the scenery is dim. The broken walls and ruins are all heartbreaking. It is difficult to recognize the old place. Everywhere, only bullet marks remain. Reluctantly tracing the battlefield, the three armies fought heroically to kill the enemy. The courage of ten thousand Japanese invaders was shattered. Their heroic deeds will be remembered for a thousand springs. Coming to lament, a hundred sorrows arise. Tears fill my blue shirt, unable to bear the sight. Leaving a few withered willows, they seem to be telling a story of parting in the rain.

Science

Methods of Water Purification

— Yun Li

Whether water is clean or not has a great impact on people's lives. Ordinary water mostly contains unclean impurities. It is unsanitary and very dangerous to life to use it as drinking water without purifying it. Therefore, if we want to drink clean water, we must go through one of the following four methods before we can have clean water to drink.

(1) Coagulation Treatment: Grind alum into a fine powder, put it into sewage, stir it evenly to dissolve it, and it will produce a gelatinous substance that combines with mud, sand, microorganisms, and all unclean impurities in the water, settling to the bottom. After two or three hours, the water will be clean and can be used as drinking water. This method is very simple and costs only one or two copper coins. Families without tap water can mostly use this method for drinking water. However, alum tastes astringent, and the amount should not be too much!

(2) Filtration: Use a pottery jar or flower pot with a hole in the bottom. Plug a sponge in the hole. Then spread a layer of charcoal chips more than an inch thick on the bottom, a layer of gravel more than an inch thick on the charcoal chips, and a layer of fine sand more than an inch thick on the gravel. Spread it in this way for several layers, and the water filter will be completed. Then pour the sewage into the jar, and in a short while, clean water will flow out from the hole in the bottom of the jar. However, the charcoal chips, fine sand, gravel, etc. in this water filter must be changed or washed frequently to prevent unclean substances and microorganisms from remaining inside.

(3) Boiling: Put the water in a pot and boil it for 15 minutes, or until the temperature reaches above 90 degrees Celsius, and the water will boil. The microorganisms in the water will not be able to survive. If this water is used as drinking water, there is no risk of causing disease. Therefore, families that want to reduce disease must implement this method for drinking water.

The above methods 1 and 2 can only remove mud and sand impurities from the water, but cannot kill the microorganisms in the water. Method 3 can only kill microorganisms, but cannot remove mud and sand. If methods 1 and 3 are used together, or methods 2 and 3 are used together, to make daily drinking water, it is very suitable. However, impurities dissolved in the water cannot be completely removed, which is indeed a common shortcoming. If you want to avoid this shortcoming and drink pure, clean water, you must use distillation.

(4) Distillation: Use a glass bottle with water filling three-fifths of the bottle. Plug the bottle mouth with a cork, and insert a curved glass tube in the middle of the cork, with one end longer and one end shorter. Next, insert the short end of the tube into the bottle, but be careful not to insert it into the bottom of the water. Extend the longer end outside the bottle. Again, put a bamboo tube on the longer end of the glass tube, and keep cold water flowing through this bamboo tube. Then put a basin under the long glass tube, and then heat the glass bottle from below with fire. When the water in the bottle boils, the steam will flow out from the glass tube and turn into water when it meets the cold in the bamboo tube, flowing into the basin. This water is distilled water. However, the cold water in the bamboo tube must be changed frequently to prevent it from becoming hot, because if it becomes hot, it will not be able to condense the steam into water. This distilled water is very hygienic. It is now used in hospitals and in the preparation of chemical medicines.

The End of the Classical Chinese Course

— Zhuo Jun

Since the abolition of the imperial examination system, private tutors have transformed into schools, allowing the academic world to conduct free research without being restricted by the poison of the eight-legged essay, which is a major liberation for education in our country.

However, what I want to talk about is the impression of the Classical Chinese course at a certain university in Shanghai and the psychology of the students.

The class bell rang, and many students in the classroom craned their necks and looked towards the classroom door, anticipating the arrival of the Classical Chinese professor, as it was the first Classical Chinese class after the start of the semester. As for the professor's name, many didn't know, so everyone wanted to catch a glimpse of the professor's demeanor and arrived very early today, almost to the point of overcrowding. Some students who arrived late were left standing outside the classroom window.

"Don't know what the surname of this teacher is?" a student nicknamed "Big Guy" asked Wang, who was sitting next to him.

"Heard it's Wang!" Wang replied uncertainly.

Before long, the Classical Chinese professor with long hair strode into the classroom, smiling at the students and saying, "Please bring your course cards for signing!" After he said this, the students swarmed forward, vying for the professor's signature, but the professor had no choice but to say, "Hand them in slowly, there's still time."

"Humph, this teacher doesn't seem fierce!" Big Guy said to the students.

"We don't have to attend classes in the future, it doesn't matter," Chen replied, seemingly echoing Big Guy's tone.

Sure enough, a week passed. Whenever it was time for the Classical Chinese class, the classroom was always very deserted. Apart from a few dozen more honest students in their seats, the rest were unwilling to attend the Classical Chinese class. They preferred to sleep or chat in their dormitories.

In dormitory number 38, Big Guy's voice spread to Wang's dormitory next door. The following is Big Guy's discussion: "Why should I study it (Classical Chinese)? It's just for these few credits; if it weren't for these few credits, I really wouldn't want to study it; we college students really don't need to study Classical Chinese; and since I'm studying banking, I need it even less."

This content was unintentionally mentioned in a conversation between my close friend Wang and me. I felt it was necessary to publish it so that readers could understand that the Classical Chinese course in universities today is merely a formality without substance. The so-called end is near. I wonder what kind of feelings the old scholars will have after reading this, or will they call it "the demise of civilization"!

Skin Color Issue

Thoughts After Reading "Attention Telephone Owners"

— Yiyi Guan Zhu

The day before yesterday (the 22nd), this newspaper's local news section published a novel news item with the title "Attention Telephone Owners," which stated:

"Recently, there has been a Chinese person between the ages of twenty-eight and thirty, about five feet seven inches tall, of medium build, with a slightly dark and round face, large and round eyes, short hair, wearing a blue cloth short jacket and pants, and a checkered cap. He can speak fluent English and specializes in going to various homes or business establishments to swindle for telephones..."

After reading the above news, the following thoughts arose:

I feel that in recent years, the number of unemployed people in society has been increasing. On the one hand, school graduates and returned students are emerging in endless streams, while on the other hand, all industries are withering, production is lagging behind, and all kinds of undertakings are stagnating. Naturally, there are not enough places to employ these batches of school graduates and returned students, and it is even more difficult for so many unemployed people to find employment. Therefore, the strong take risks, and the weak become pessimistic or have wild ideas, engaging in various kinds of deceptive activities, such as the swindler who specializes in defrauding people of their telephones. Could he not be one of them? Although his attire resembles that of a worker, since he can speak fluent English, we assume that even if he is not a returned student, he must be a graduate of some school. I believe that this kind of swindler should not only be paid attention to by telephone owners, but also by important figures in society.

A Corner of Society

Standing Guard

— Tan Zhuoming

This is the XX Company's warehouse! A three-story "Shanghai-style" house, with goods piled up on the second floor and downstairs, and the third floor used as a dormitory for the staff. The kitchen downstairs is designated as the office and residence of the warehouse manager L. The room contains only a square table and a board bed, the furnishings are very simple. Because of the water pipes on the wall, the ground is very damp, and it is covered with thick phlegm, so it is wet and sticky. It is dusk, and five or six people are distributed on the board bed and around the table. Several people are smoking cigarettes, and wisps of white smoke spew out from everyone's mouths, enveloping the room in a thick white mist.

"Going out to have fun?" L asked strangely, seeing that they hadn't gone out these past few days.

"Ugh! Where is there to go? Anlewo (entertainment venue) is closed, Liyuan Company is closed, the area around the Great World is as desolate as death, who would be happy to go out?" B sighed deeply.

"Let's do it ourselves, mahjong, poker, whatever you like," T, a poker expert, proposed at the opportunity.

"No, it's too dangerous, what if the boss sees it? It won't be good for anyone," L vehemently objected because he was responsible for the security here.

"Find someone to stand guard."

"Idiot, how can you transmit messages across two floors?"

"Ugh: : :"

Everyone felt that there was no way to "stand guard," a look of disappointment on their faces, and remained silent. The room was silent.

K is the accountant of this company, very clever and resourceful. The boss trusts him very much. He likes to drink, but he is not very willing to spend his own money to buy it. If his colleagues have something to ask him to solve, they only need to treat him to a meal, and he will gladly help. Over time, it has become a kind of trade. Now, seeing that the opportunity has come, he frowned, scratched his hair, and asked for a meal as the price. After a while, he smiled slightly and said:

"If you can treat me to a meal, I'll give you a very good "guarding method."

Everyone's eyes focused on K's face. K smiled and said nothing. T knew this was his old habit, reached into his pocket, took out two silver dollars, and slammed them on the table with a "bang"!

"Tell me, if it's applicable, this is the reward."

"This method is very easy. Tomorrow, I'll tell the boss: "The people in the dormitory are too lazy, and they often forget to turn off the lights when they go to bed. It's best to install the electricity meter in L's room and have L be responsible for turning it on and off every night. I think the boss will definitely agree. The matter will be successful. When the boss comes, just turn the electricity meter a few times, won't the lights upstairs flicker?"

"Great plan, let's go, let's go drink a big cup," T took the two silver dollars on the table and left first, with everyone cheering and following him out of the room.

From then on, the boss often praised his employees to others, saying:

"Every time I go to the dormitory to inspect, all the employees are reading or writing."

Reversing the Car

New Invention of the Chinese People

— Yu Jianhua

Since ancient times, the Chinese people have invented countless good things. Now, the ability to invent is even more developed, especially our government authorities, who are almost racking their brains every day to come up with new ideas. They are truly worthy of being the Edisons of the East.

Last year, our young marshal invented "non-resistance," and lightly gave away the three northeastern provinces. This year, the old comrades invented "long-term resistance," and almost lightly gave away Songhu.

At the beginning of the Shanghai Incident, they invented "not losing an inch of land," but later found that it was not enough, so they invented "strategic retreat, to the second line of defense." Our "national light" initially invented "vowing to defend the country," and later invented "preserving strength," then invented "acting insincerely," then invented "vowing to fight to the death," and now they are probably inventing "gathering for a counterattack."

After the government abolished the likin (internal transit tax), it then invented the "business tax." Now, because it cannot collect the national taxes from the three northeastern provinces and Guangdong and Guangxi, the clever uncle is about to invent some kind of "new tax" in addition to miscellaneous levies and taxes.

After already banning opium, they invented "imposing a tax in the guise of prohibition," and now they have invented "government monopoly." Just as the X Concession was about to ban opium, someone had already invented a "security company" to contract and seize contributions.

With so many inventors and such wonderful inventions, in just a few years, why worry that China will not become a first-class power?

Mischief

An Inhuman Act of Violence

— Shi Ben

Last month, Mr. Leshan's article (A Maid's Confession) in this publication already fully revealed the suffering of maids in the world. But now, there is an even worse case of abuse than others, which I have personally witnessed and heard about. I am writing to this publication to show that this inhuman behavior actually exists in this era that sings the praises of humanitarianism and claims to be civilized.

In our town, there is a wealthy household. The master is an old man over seventy years old. Although this old man is so old, his spirit is better than that of us young people. His skin is smooth and ruddy, and he doesn't walk with any signs of old age. The neighbors, seeing that he is so hale and hearty, all went to ask him the secret of his health, but strangely, no matter how they asked, he always refused to reveal his secret to good health. Some suspected that he was taking tonics such as ginseng and bird's nest. Originally, people like this who were rich and powerful naturally had enough ginseng and bird's nest to eat constantly. Therefore, others, seeing that he was unwilling to reveal the reason, stopped asking and firmly believed in the effectiveness of his taking ginseng and bird's nest. But I had some doubts, thinking that since he had gained effectiveness from taking ginseng and bird's nest, then this was a legitimate health technique, and there was definitely no hidden secret. One day, it happened that one of his maids came to my house to borrow something, so I inquired with her. She said: This old man has a strange temperament and likes to buy young maids. There are often more than a dozen in his house. These young maids are bought not for work, but entirely for his personal health. He uses one of the maids every night and gives her a black date every night. When dawn comes (please excuse me for not explaining this here), he steams the black date and eats it. He has been doing this every day for more than ten years. After being subjected to this treatment, these maids gradually lose their essence, become sallow and emaciated, and most of them die within two or three years. Alas! Over the past ten years, he has killed quite a few people!

Oh dear! After listening to her words, I couldn't help but feel my hair stand on end. No wonder he is so healthy and can't say why he is so healthy. It turns out that he is using this inhuman method of harming others to benefit himself, like a demon extracting human essence. Alas! His life is not maintained by "vitamins," but simply by harming her life to "vitaminize" him.

Criminal Judgment: Lu Anbo v. Gu Hailin: Case of Destruction and Abandonment (Main Text): This private prosecution is not accepted. ▲ Chen Xiaoerzi's Theft Case (Main Text): Chen Xiaoerzi is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for committing theft in a group of three or more. Two days of detention shall be counted as one day of imprisonment. ▲ Wu Danshi et al.: Case of Disruption of Family and Fraud (Main Text): Wu Danshi is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for enticing a woman under the age of twenty away from her guardian with intent to profit. He is also sentenced to two months of imprisonment for obtaining another person's property through fraudulent means. The fixed term of imprisonment is one year and one month. Two days of detention shall be counted as one day of imprisonment. Dai Rong is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for harboring an abducted person with intent to commit adultery. Two days of detention shall be counted as one day of imprisonment. ▲ Wu Danshi shall pay Yang Minshi one hundred and fifteen yuan and two jiao to collect. The remaining parts of the incidental civil action are dismissed. ▲ Hua Kaizhu et al.: Case of Public Endangerment (Main Text): Hua Kaizhu is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for attempted arson of another person's residence that is not currently in use. Two days of detention shall be counted as one day of imprisonment. Xia Guangrong is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for inciting another person to commit attempted arson of another person's residence that is not currently in use. Two days of detention shall be counted as one day of imprisonment. Six rolls of gunpowder are confiscated.

Criminal Ruling: Chen Shijie's order for his wife to cohabitate is noted. As the case is a civil matter, he should file a lawsuit in the Civil Division. ▲ Xi Yushu et al.'s petition to be given the Songjiang Bank receipts is noted. It has been verified that the relevant receipts were previously investigated by Attorney Jin Yu and Xia Run in the case. Upon completion of the verification, it coincided with the end-of-year closing period, and for the sake of facilitating liquidation, they were returned to Jin Yu to retrieve and agreed to be transferred to the accountant. Recently, the Songjiang County Court has entrusted the safekeeping of all receipts and items of the Shanghai Songjiang Bank to this office. As the guaranteed part is purely within the civil scope, it has been transferred to the Civil Division of this court for handling. If there are any further issues, please make a request to that division. ▲ Yu Lvshi's semi-complaint against Shan Jichun's defense is noted. It has already been clarified in Shan Jibiao's petition.
